	endorse Obama, and she and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> gave convention
	speeches in his support.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-delegates-185">[185]</a> Obama
	delivered his acceptance speech, not at the center where the Democratic National Convention was held, but at <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invesco_Field_at_Mile_High">Invesco Field at Mile High</a> to a crowd of
	approximately 84,000 people; the speech was viewed by over 38&nbsp;million people worldwide.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-npr1409-186">[186]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-acceptance-187">[187]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-188">[188]</a></p>

<p>During both the primary process and the general election, Obama's campaign set numerous fundraising records,
	particularly in the quantity of small donations.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-small_donations-189">[189]</a> On June 19, 2008,
	Obama became the first major-party presidential candidate to turn down <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campaign_finance_in_the_United_States#Public_financing_of_campaigns">public
		financing</a> in the general election since the system was created in 1976.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Bloomberg_Salant_20080619-190">[190]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/ElectoralCollege2008.svg/280px-ElectoralCollege2008.svg.png"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/ElectoralCollege2008.svg/420px-ElectoralCollege2008.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/ElectoralCollege2008.svg/560px-ElectoralCollege2008.svg.png 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="280"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>2008 electoral vote results</p>

<p>John McCain was nominated as the Republican candidate, and he selected <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarah_Palin">Sarah Palin</a> as his running mate. The two candidates engaged
	in three <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_debates">presidential
		debates</a> in September and October 2008.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-presidential_debates-191">[191]</a> On November 4,
	Obama won the presidency with 365 <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)">electoral votes</a> to 173 received by
	McCain.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-electoral_votes-192">[192]</a> Obama won 52.9%
	of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Election">popular vote</a> to McCain's 45.7%.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-193">[193]</a> He became the first African American
	to be elected president.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-194">[194]</a> Obama delivered
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama_election_victory_speech,_2008">his victory speech</a> before
	hundreds of thousands of supporters in Chicago's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grant_Park_(Chicago)">Grant
		Park</a>.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-independent1-195">[195]</a></p>
<h3><strong>2012</strong></h3>

<p><i>Main articles: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_United_States_presidential_election"><i>2012 United
			States presidential election</i></a><i> and </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama_2012_presidential_campaign"><i>Barack Obama 2012 presidential
			campaign</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/P112912PS-0444_-_President_Barack_Obama_and_Mitt_Romney_in_the_Oval_Office_-_crop.jpg/220px-P112912PS-0444_-_President_Barack_Obama_and_Mitt_Romney_in_the_Oval_Office_-_crop.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/P112912PS-0444_-_President_Barack_Obama_and_Mitt_Romney_in_the_Oval_Office_-_crop.jpg/330px-P112912PS-0444_-_President_Barack_Obama_and_Mitt_Romney_in_the_Oval_Office_-_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/P112912PS-0444_-_President_Barack_Obama_and_Mitt_Romney_in_the_Oval_Office_-_crop.jpg/440px-P112912PS-0444_-_President_Barack_Obama_and_Mitt_Romney_in_the_Oval_Office_-_crop.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama greets former Governor <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitt_Romney">Mitt Romney</a> in the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oval_Office">Oval Office</a> on November 29, 2012, in their first meeting
	since Obama's re-election victory over Romney.</p>

<p>On April 4, 2011, Obama announced his reelection campaign for 2012 in a video titled "It Begins with Us" that he
	posted on his website and filed election papers with the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Election_Commission">Federal Election Commission</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-196">[196]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-197">[197]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-198">[198]</a> As the incumbent president he ran
	virtually unopposed in the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries,_2012">Democratic Party presidential
		primaries</a>,<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-CNN-clinch1-199">[199]</a> and on
	April 3, 2012, Obama had secured the 2778 <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Democratic_National_Convention">convention</a> delegates needed to win
	the Democratic nomination.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-CNN-clinch2-200">[200]</a>
</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/ElectoralCollege2012.svg/280px-ElectoralCollege2012.svg.png"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/ElectoralCollege2012.svg/420px-ElectoralCollege2012.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/ElectoralCollege2012.svg/560px-ElectoralCollege2012.svg.png 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="280"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>2012 electoral vote results</p>

<p>At the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Democratic_National_Convention">Democratic National Convention</a>
	in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a>, Obama and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden">Joe Biden</a> were formally nominated by former President <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> as the Democratic Party candidates for
	president and vice president in the general election. Their main opponents were Republicans <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitt_Romney">Mitt Romney</a>, the former governor of Massachusetts, and
	Representative <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Ryan">Paul Ryan</a> of Wisconsin.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-201">[201]</a></p>

<p>On November 6, 2012, Obama won 332 <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)">electoral votes</a>, exceeding the 270
	required for him to be reelected as president.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-202">[202]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-203">[203]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-204">[204]</a> With 51.1% of the popular vote,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-FEC-205">[205]</a> Obama became the first Democratic
	president since <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> to win the
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_presidential_elections_by_popular_vote_margin">majority
		of the popular vote</a> twice.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-206">[206]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-207">[207]</a> Obama addressed supporters and
	volunteers at Chicago's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McCormick_Place">McCormick Place</a> after his
	reelection and said: "Tonight you voted for action, not politics as usual. You elected us to focus on your jobs, not
	ours. And in the coming weeks and months, I am looking forward to reaching out and working with leaders of both
	parties."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-208">[208]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-NYT20130121-209">[209]</a></p>
<h2>Presidency (2009–2017)</h2>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidency_of_Barack_Obama"><i>Presidency of Barack
			Obama</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><i>For a chronological guide to this subject, see </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Presidency_of_Barack_Obama"><i>Timeline of the Presidency of
			Barack Obama</i></a><i>.</i></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><i>See also: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confirmations_of_Barack_Obama%27s_Cabinet"><i>Confirmations
			of Barack Obama's Cabinet</i></a><i> and </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_international_presidential_trips_made_by_Barack_Obama"><i>List of
			international presidential trips made by Barack Obama</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<h3><strong>First 100 days</strong></h3>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_100_days_of_Barack_Obama%27s_presidency"><i>First
			100 days of Barack Obama's presidency</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/US_President_Barack_Obama_taking_his_Oath_of_Office_-_2009Jan20.jpg/220px-US_President_Barack_Obama_taking_his_Oath_of_Office_-_2009Jan20.jpg"
		alt="Photograph"
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/US_President_Barack_Obama_taking_his_Oath_of_Office_-_2009Jan20.jpg/330px-US_President_Barack_Obama_taking_his_Oath_of_Office_-_2009Jan20.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/US_President_Barack_Obama_taking_his_Oath_of_Office_-_2009Jan20.jpg/440px-US_President_Barack_Obama_taking_his_Oath_of_Office_-_2009Jan20.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Barack Obama takes <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oath_of_office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States">the
		oath of office</a> administered by <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States">Chief Justice</a> <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Roberts">John G. Roberts Jr.</a> at <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Capitol">the Capitol</a>, January 20, 2009</p>

<p>The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Barack_Obama">inauguration of Barack Obama</a> as
	the 44th President took place on January 20, 2009. In his first few days in office, Obama issued <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_order">executive orders</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_memorandum">presidential memoranda</a> directing the U.S.
	military to develop plans to withdraw troops from Iraq.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-210">[210]</a> He ordered the closing of the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_detention_camp">Guantanamo Bay detention camp</a>,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-211">[211]</a> but Congress prevented the closure by
	refusing to appropriate the required funds<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-212">[212]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-213">[213]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-214">[214]</a> and preventing moving any Guantanamo
	detainee into the U.S. or to other countries.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-215">[215]</a> Obama reduced the secrecy given to
	presidential records.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-216">[216]</a> He also revoked
	President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_W._Bush">George W. Bush</a>'s restoration of President <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>'s <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico_City_Policy">Mexico City Policy</a> prohibiting federal aid to
	international family planning organizations that perform or provide counseling about abortion.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-217">[217]</a></p>
<h3><strong>Domestic policy</strong></h3>

<p><i>See also: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_policy_of_the_Barack_Obama_administration"><i>Social
			policy of the Barack Obama administration</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>The first bill signed into law by Obama was the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lilly_Ledbetter_Fair_Pay_Act_of_2009">Lilly Ledbetter Fair Pay Act of
		2009</a>, relaxing the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statute_of_limitations">statute of limitations</a>
	for equal-pay lawsuits.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-218">[218]</a> Five days later,
	he signed the reauthorization of the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_Children%27s_Health_Insurance_Program">State Children's Health
		Insurance Program</a> (SCHIP) to cover an additional 4&nbsp;million uninsured children.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-219">[219]</a> In March 2009, Obama reversed a
	Bush-era policy that had limited funding of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryonic_stem_cell">embryonic
		stem cell</a> research and pledged to develop "strict guidelines" on the research.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-220">[220]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Barack_Obama_addresses_joint_session_of_Congress_2009-02-24.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_addresses_joint_session_of_Congress_2009-02-24.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Barack_Obama_addresses_joint_session_of_Congress_2009-02-24.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_addresses_joint_session_of_Congress_2009-02-24.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Barack_Obama_addresses_joint_session_of_Congress_2009-02-24.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_addresses_joint_session_of_Congress_2009-02-24.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama delivers a <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama_speech_to_joint_session_of_Congress,_February_2009">speech at
		joint session of Congress</a> with Vice President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden">Joe
		Biden</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives">House Speaker</a> <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nancy_Pelosi">Nancy Pelosi</a> on February 24, 2009.</p>

<p>Obama appointed two women to serve on the Supreme Court in the first two years of his Presidency. He nominated <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonia_Sotomayor">Sonia Sotomayor</a> on May 26, 2009 to replace retiring <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Associate_Justice_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States">Associate
		Justice</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Souter">David Souter</a>; she was confirmed on August
	6, 2009,<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-221">[221]</a> becoming the first Supreme
	Court Justice of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hispanic">Hispanic</a> descent.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-222">[222]</a> Obama nominated <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elena_Kagan">Elena Kagan</a> on May 10, 2010 to replace retiring Associate
	Justice <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Paul_Stevens">John Paul Stevens</a>. She was confirmed on August
	5, 2010, bringing the number of women sitting simultaneously on the Court to three justices for the first time in
	American history.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-223">[223]</a></p>

<p>On March 30, 2010, Obama signed the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_Care_and_Education_Reconciliation_Act_of_2010">Health Care and
		Education Reconciliation Act</a>, a <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconciliation_(United_States_Congress)">reconciliation bill</a> that ended
	the process of the federal government giving subsidies to private banks to give out federally insured loans,
	increased the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pell_Grant">Pell Grant</a> scholarship award, and made changes
	to the Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-224">[224]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-225">[225]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Obama_cabinet_meeting_2009-11.jpg/220px-Obama_cabinet_meeting_2009-11.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Obama_cabinet_meeting_2009-11.jpg/330px-Obama_cabinet_meeting_2009-11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Obama_cabinet_meeting_2009-11.jpg/440px-Obama_cabinet_meeting_2009-11.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama meets with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_States">Cabinet of the United
		States</a>, November 23, 2009.</p>

<p>In a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_policy_of_the_Barack_Obama_administration">major space policy
		speech</a> in April 2010, Obama announced a planned change in direction at <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA">NASA</a>, the U.S. space agency. He ended plans for a return of <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_spaceflight">human spaceflight</a> to the moon and development of the
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ares_I">Ares I</a> rocket, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ares_V">Ares V</a> rocket and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constellation_program">Constellation program</a>, in favor of funding Earth
	science projects, a new rocket type, and research and development for an eventual manned mission to Mars, and
	ongoing missions to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Space_Station">International Space
		Station</a>.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-226">[226]</a></p>

<p>President Obama's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_State_of_the_Union_Address">2011 State of the Union
		Address</a> focused on themes of education and innovation, stressing the importance of <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Innovation_economics">innovation economics</a> to make the United States
	more competitive globally. He spoke of a five-year freeze in domestic spending, eliminating tax breaks for oil
	companies and reversing tax cuts for the wealthiest Americans, banning congressional <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earmark_(politics)">earmarks</a>, and reducing healthcare costs. He promised
	the United States would have one million electric vehicles on the road by 2015 and be 80% reliant on "<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sustainable_energy">clean</a>" electricity.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-227">[227]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-228">[228]</a></p>
<h4><strong>LGBT rights</strong></h4>

<p>On October 8, 2009, Obama signed the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthew_Shepard_and_James_Byrd_Jr._Hate_Crimes_Prevention_Act">Matthew
		Shepard and James Byrd Jr. Hate Crimes Prevention Act</a>, a measure that expanded the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hate_crime_laws_in_the_United_States#Federal_prosecution_of_hate_crimes">1969
		United States federal hate-crime law</a> to include crimes motivated by a victim's actual or perceived gender,
	sexual orientation, gender identity, or disability.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-229">[229]</a></p>

<p>On October 30, 2009, Obama lifted the ban on travel to the United States by those infected with <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HIV">HIV</a>, which was celebrated by <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_Equality">Immigration Equality</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-230">[230]</a></p>

<p>On December 22, 2010, Obama signed the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don%27t_Ask,_Don%27t_Tell_Repeal_Act_of_2010">Don't Ask, Don't Tell Repeal
		Act of 2010</a>, which fulfilled a key promise made in the 2008 presidential campaign<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-231">[231]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-232">[232]</a> to end the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don%27t_ask,_don%27t_tell">Don't ask, don't tell</a> policy of 1993 that had
	prevented gay and lesbian people from serving openly in the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces">United States Armed Forces</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-233">[233]</a> In 2016, the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Pentagon">Pentagon</a> also ended the policy that barred <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transgender">transgender</a> people from serving openly in the military.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-TransBan1-234">[234]</a></p>

<p>As a candidate for the Illinois state senate in 1996, Obama had said he favored legalizing <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_States">same-sex marriage</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-WCT0114-235">[235]</a> By the time of his Senate run
	in 2004, he said he supported civil unions and domestic partnerships for same-sex partners but opposed same-sex
	marriages.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-WCT0204-236">[236]</a> In 2008, he
	reaffirmed this position by stating "I believe marriage is between a man and a woman. I am not in favor of gay
	marriage."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-237">[237]</a> On May 9, 2012, shortly after
	the official launch of his campaign for re-election as president, Obama said his views had evolved, and he publicly
	affirmed his personal support for the legalization of same-sex marriage, becoming the first sitting U.S. president
	to do so.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-238">[238]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-The_Huffington_Post-239">[239]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Celebrating_a_new_America_-lovewins_58242_%2818588276403%29.jpg/220px-Celebrating_a_new_America_-lovewins_58242_%2818588276403%29.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Celebrating_a_new_America_-lovewins_58242_%2818588276403%29.jpg/330px-Celebrating_a_new_America_-lovewins_58242_%2818588276403%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Celebrating_a_new_America_-lovewins_58242_%2818588276403%29.jpg/440px-Celebrating_a_new_America_-lovewins_58242_%2818588276403%29.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House">White House</a> was illuminated in rainbow colors on the
	evening of the Supreme Court same-sex marriage ruling, June 26, 2015.</p>

<p>During his second <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_inauguration_of_Barack_Obama">inaugural address</a>
	on January 21, 2013,<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-NYT20130121-209">[209]</a> Obama
	became the first U.S. President in office to call for full equality for gay Americans: "Our journey is not complete
	until our gay brothers and sisters are treated like anyone else under the law—for if we are truly created equal,
	then surely the love we commit to one another must be equal as well." This was the first time that a president
	mentioned <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_States">gay rights</a> or the word "gay"
	in an inaugural address.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-240">[240]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-241">[241]</a></p>

<p>In 2013, the Obama Administration filed briefs that urged the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States">Supreme Court</a> to rule in favor of
	same-sex couples in the cases of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollingsworth_v._Perry"><i>Hollingsworth v.
			Perry</i></a> (regarding <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_States">same-sex marriage</a>)<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-huffpo-amicus-242">[242]</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_v._Windsor"><i>United States v. Windsor</i></a> (regarding the
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defense_of_Marriage_Act">Defense of Marriage Act</a>).<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-cnn-amicus-243">[243]</a> Then, following the Supreme
	Court's 2015 decision in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obergefell_v._Hodges"><i>Obergefell v.
			Hodges</i></a> (ruling same-sex marriage to be a fundamental right), Obama asserted that, "This decision
	affirms what millions of Americans already believe in their hearts: When all Americans are treated as equal we are
	all more free."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-remarksDecision-244">[244]</a></p>

<p>On July 30, 2015, the White House Office of National AIDS Policy revised its strategy for addressing the disease,
	which included widespread testing and linkage to healthcare, which was celebrated by the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Rights_Campaign">Human Rights Campaign</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-245">[245]</a></p>
<h4><strong>White House advisory and oversight groups</strong></h4>

<p>On March 11, 2009, Obama created the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Council_on_Women_and_Girls">White House Council on Women and
		Girls</a>, which formed part of the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Office_of_Intergovernmental_Affairs">Office of Intergovernmental
		Affairs</a>, having been established by <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_order_(United_States)">Executive Order</a> <a
		href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Executive_Order_13506">13506</a> with a broad mandate to advise him on
	issues relating to the welfare of American women and girls.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Executive-246">[246]</a> The Council was chaired by
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senior_Advisor_to_the_President">Senior Advisor to the President</a> <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valerie_Jarrett">Valerie Jarrett</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Sexualassault-247">[247]</a> Obama also established
	the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Task_Force_to_Protect_Students_from_Sexual_Assault">White
		House Task Force to Protect Students from Sexual Assault</a> through a government memorandum on January 22,
	2014, with a broad mandate to advise him on issues relating to sexual assault on college and university campuses
	throughout the United States.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Sexualassault-247">[247]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Memo-248">[248]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Freedom-249">[249]</a> The co-chairs of the Task
	Force were Vice President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden">Joe Biden</a> and Jarrett.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Memo-248">[248]</a> The Task Force was a development
	out of the White House Council on Women and Girls and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Office_of_the_Vice_President_of_the_United_States">Office of the Vice
		President of the United States</a>, and prior to that the 1994 <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violence_Against_Women_Act">Violence Against Women Act</a> first drafted by
	Biden.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Report-250">[250]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Economic policy</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_policy_of_the_Barack_Obama_administration"><i>Economic policy of
			the Barack Obama administration</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/20090124_WeeklyAddress.ogv/220px-seek%3D63-20090124_WeeklyAddress.ogv.jpg"
		alt="File:20090124 WeeklyAddress.ogv"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama presents his first <a
		href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Obama_Administration_weekly_video_addresses">weekly address</a> as
	President of the United States on January 24, 2009, discussing the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Recovery_and_Reinvestment_Act_of_2009">American Recovery and
		Reinvestment Act of 2009</a></p>

<p>On February 17, 2009, Obama signed the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Recovery_and_Reinvestment_Act_of_2009">American Recovery and
		Reinvestment Act of 2009</a>, a $787&nbsp;billion <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stimulus_(economics)">economic stimulus</a> package aimed at helping the
	economy recover from the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Recession">deepening worldwide
		recession</a>.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-251">[251]</a> The act includes
	increased federal spending for health care, infrastructure, education, various tax breaks and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_incentive">incentives</a>, and direct assistance to individuals.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-direct_assistance-252">[252]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/U.S._Total_Deficits_vs._National_Debt_Increases_2001-2010.png/220px-U.S._Total_Deficits_vs._National_Debt_Increases_2001-2010.png"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/U.S._Total_Deficits_vs._National_Debt_Increases_2001-2010.png/330px-U.S._Total_Deficits_vs._National_Debt_Increases_2001-2010.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/U.S._Total_Deficits_vs._National_Debt_Increases_2001-2010.png/440px-U.S._Total_Deficits_vs._National_Debt_Increases_2001-2010.png 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_federal_budget">Deficit</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_debt_of_the_United_States">debt</a> increases, 2001–16</p>

<p>In March, Obama's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treasury_Secretary">Treasury Secretary</a>, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timothy_Geithner">Timothy Geithner</a>, took further steps to manage the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308">financial crisis</a>, including
	introducing the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public%E2%80%93Private_Investment_Program_for_Legacy_Assets">Public–Private
		Investment Program for Legacy Assets</a>, which contains provisions for buying up to two&nbsp;trillion dollars
	in depreciated real estate assets.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-markets_opened-253">[253]</a></p>

<p>Obama intervened in the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automotive_industry_crisis_of_2008%E2%80%9310">troubled automotive
		industry</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-254">[254]</a> in March 2009, renewing
	loans for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Motors">General Motors</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chrysler">Chrysler</a> to continue operations while reorganizing. Over the
	following months the White House set terms for both firms' bankruptcies, including the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chrysler_Chapter_11_reorganization">sale of Chrysler</a> to Italian
	automaker <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiat">Fiat</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-255">[255]</a> and a <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Motors_Chapter_11_reorganization">reorganization of GM</a> giving
	the U.S. government a temporary 60% equity stake in the company, with the Canadian government taking a 12% stake.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-256">[256]</a> In June 2009, dissatisfied with the
	pace of economic stimulus, Obama called on his cabinet to accelerate the investment.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Christopher_Conkey_and_Louise_Radnofsky-257">[257]</a>
	He signed into law the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Car_Allowance_Rebate_System">Car Allowance Rebate
		System</a>, known colloquially as "Cash for Clunkers," which temporarily boosted the economy.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-258">[258]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-259">[259]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-260">[260]</a></p>

<p>The Bush and Obama administrations authorized spending and loan guarantees from the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Reserve_System">Federal Reserve</a> and the Treasury Department.
	These guarantees totaled about $11.5&nbsp;trillion, but only $3&nbsp;trillion had been spent by the end of November
	2009.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-261">[261]</a> Obama and the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congressional_Budget_Office">Congressional Budget Office</a> predicted the
	2010 <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_United_States_federal_budget">budget deficit</a> would be
	$1.5&nbsp;trillion or 10.6% of the nation's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_domestic_product">gross
		domestic product</a> (GDP) compared to the 2009 deficit of $1.4&nbsp;trillion or 9.9% of GDP.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-262">[262]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-263">[263]</a> For 2011, the administration predicted
	the deficit would shrink to $1.34&nbsp;trillion, and the 10-year deficit would increase to $8.53&nbsp;trillion or
	90% of GDP.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-264">[264]</a> The most recent increase in
	the U.S. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_debt_ceiling">debt ceiling</a> to $17.2&nbsp;trillion
	took effect in February 2014.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-265">[265]</a> On August
	2, 2011, after a lengthy congressional debate over whether to raise the nation's debt limit, Obama signed the
	bipartisan <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Budget_Control_Act_of_2011">Budget Control Act of 2011</a>. The
	legislation enforces limits on discretionary spending until 2021, establishes a procedure to increase the debt
	limit, creates a Congressional Joint Select Committee on Deficit Reduction to propose further deficit reduction with
	a stated goal of achieving at least $1.5&nbsp;trillion in budgetary savings over 10 years, and establishes automatic
	procedures for reducing spending by as much as $1.2&nbsp;trillion if legislation originating with the new joint
	select committee does not achieve such savings.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-266">[266]</a> By passing the legislation, Congress
	was able to prevent a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States">U.S.
		government</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Default_(finance)">default</a> on its obligations.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-267">[267]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/US_Employment_Statistics.svg/300px-US_Employment_Statistics.svg.png"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/US_Employment_Statistics.svg/450px-US_Employment_Statistics.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/US_Employment_Statistics.svg/600px-US_Employment_Statistics.svg.png 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="300"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>US employment statistics (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unemployment_rate">unemployment rate</a> and monthly
	changes in net employment) during Obama's tenure as U.S. President<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-268">[268]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-269">[269]</a></p>

<p>As it did throughout 2008, the unemployment rate rose in 2009, reaching a peak in October at 10.0% and averaging
	10.0% in the fourth quarter. Following a decrease to 9.7% in the first quarter of 2010, the unemployment rate fell
	to 9.6% in the second quarter, where it remained for the rest of the year.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Theodossiou-270">[270]</a> Between February and
	December 2010, employment rose by 0.8%, which was less than the average of 1.9% experienced during comparable
	periods in the past four employment recoveries.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Eddlemon-271">[271]</a> By November 2012, the
	unemployment rate fell to 7.7%,<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-272">[272]</a>
	decreasing to 6.7% in the last month of 2013.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-273">[273]</a> During 2014, the unemployment rate
	continued to decline, falling to 6.3% in the first quarter.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-274">[274]</a> GDP growth returned in the third
	quarter of 2009, expanding at a rate of 1.6%, followed by a 5.0% increase in the fourth quarter.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-BEA1-275">[275]</a> Growth continued in 2010, posting
	an increase of 3.7% in the first quarter, with lesser gains throughout the rest of the year.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-BEA1-275">[275]</a> In July 2010, the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Reserve_System">Federal Reserve</a> noted that economic activity
	continued to increase, but its pace had slowed, and chairman <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Bernanke">Ben Bernanke</a> said the economic outlook was "unusually
	uncertain."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-276">[276]</a> Overall, the economy
	expanded at a rate of 2.9% in 2010.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-277">[277]</a></p>

<p>The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congressional_Budget_Office">Congressional Budget Office</a> (CBO) and a
	broad range of economists credit Obama's stimulus plan for economic growth.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-estimated-278">[278]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-newc-279">[279]</a> The CBO released a report stating
	that the stimulus bill increased employment by 1–2.1&nbsp;million,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-newc-279">[279]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-280">[280]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-281">[281]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-282">[282]</a> while conceding that "It is impossible
	to determine how many of the reported jobs would have existed in the absence of the stimulus package."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-estimated-278">[278]</a> Although an April 2010,
	survey of members of the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Association_for_Business_Economics">National Association for
		Business Economics</a> showed an increase in job creation (over a similar January survey) for the first time in
	two years, 73% of 68 respondents believed the stimulus bill has had no impact on employment.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-283">[283]</a> The economy of the United States has
	grown faster than the other original <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO">NATO</a> members by a wider margin
	under President Obama than it has anytime since the end of <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II">World War II</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-284">[284]</a> The <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> credits the
	much faster growth in the United States to the stimulus plan of the US and the austerity measures in the European
	Union.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-285">[285]</a></p>

<p>Within a month of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_United_States_elections">2010 midterm
		elections</a>, Obama announced a compromise deal with the Congressional Republican leadership that included a
	temporary, two-year extension of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bush_tax_cuts">2001 and 2003 income tax
		rates</a>, a one-year <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Insurance_Contributions_Act_tax">payroll
		tax</a> reduction, continuation of unemployment benefits, and a new rate and exemption amount for <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estate_tax_in_the_United_States">estate taxes</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-286">[286]</a> The compromise overcame opposition
	from some in both parties, and the resulting $858&nbsp;billion <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_Relief,_Unemployment_Insurance_Reauthorization,_and_Job_Creation_Act_of_2010">Tax
		Relief, Unemployment Insurance Reauthorization, and Job Creation Act of 2010</a> passed with bipartisan
	majorities in both houses of Congress before Obama signed it on December 17, 2010.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-287">[287]</a></p>

<p>In December 2013, Obama declared that growing <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Income_inequality_in_the_United_States">income inequality</a> is a "defining
	challenge of our time" and called on Congress to bolster the safety net and raise wages. This came on the heels of
	the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fast_food_worker_strikes">nationwide strikes of fast-food workers</a> and
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Francis">Pope Francis</a>' criticism of inequality and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trickle-down_economics">trickle-down economics</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-288">[288]</a></p>

<p>Obama urged Congress to ratify a 12-nation free trade pact called the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Partnership">Trans-Pacific Partnership</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-289">[289]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Environmental policy</strong></h4>

<p><i>See also: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_policy_of_the_United_States"><i>Climate change
			policy of the United States</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Obama-venice-la.jpg/220px-Obama-venice-la.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Obama-venice-la.jpg/330px-Obama-venice-la.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Obama-venice-la.jpg/440px-Obama-venice-la.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama at a 2010 briefing on the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BP_oil_spill">BP oil spill</a> at the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard">Coast Guard</a> Station Venice in <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venice,_Louisiana">Venice, Louisiana</a></p>

<p>On September 30, 2009, the Obama administration proposed new regulations on power plants, factories, and oil
	refineries in an attempt to limit greenhouse gas emissions and to curb <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_warming">global warming</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-290">[290]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-291">[291]</a></p>

<p>On April 20, 2010, an explosion destroyed an offshore <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drilling_rig">drilling
		rig</a> at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macondo_Prospect">Macondo Prospect</a> in the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, causing a <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill">major sustained oil leak</a>. Obama visited the
	Gulf, announced a federal investigation, and formed a bipartisan commission to recommend new safety standards, after
	a review by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Interior">Secretary of the
		Interior</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ken_Salazar">Ken Salazar</a> and concurrent Congressional
	hearings. He then announced a six-month moratorium on new <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deepwater_drilling">deepwater drilling</a> permits and leases, pending
	regulatory review.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-292">[292]</a> As multiple efforts
	by BP failed, some in the media and public expressed confusion and criticism over various aspects of the incident,
	and stated a desire for more involvement by Obama and the federal government.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-293">[293]</a></p>

<p>In July 2013, Obama expressed reservations and said he "would reject the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keystone_XL_pipeline">Keystone XL pipeline</a> if it increased carbon
	pollution" or "greenhouse emissions."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-294">[294]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-295">[295]</a> Obama's advisers called for a halt to
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petroleum_exploration_in_the_Arctic">petroleum exploration in the Arctic</a>
	in January 2013.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-296">[296]</a> On February 24, 2015,
	Obama vetoed a bill that would have authorized the pipeline.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-297">[297]</a> It was the third veto of Obama's
	presidency and his first major veto.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-298">[298]</a></p>

<p>Obama emphasized the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservation_movement">conservation</a> of <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_lands">federal lands</a> during his term in office. He used his
	power under the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antiquities_Act">Antiquities Act</a> to create 25 new <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_monument_(United_States)">national monuments</a> during his
	presidency and expand four others, protecting a total of 553,000,000 acres (224,000,000&nbsp;ha) of federal lands
	and waters, more than any other U.S. president.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Monuments-299">[299]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-300">[300]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-301">[301]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-302">[302]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Health care reform</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_care_reform_in_the_United_States"><i>Health care
			reform in the United States</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Obama_signs_health_care-20100323.jpg/220px-Obama_signs_health_care-20100323.jpg"
		alt="Photograph"
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Obama_signs_health_care-20100323.jpg/330px-Obama_signs_health_care-20100323.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Obama_signs_health_care-20100323.jpg/440px-Obama_signs_health_care-20100323.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama signs the Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act at the White House, March 23, 2010.</p>

<p>Obama called for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress">Congress</a> to pass legislation
	reforming <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_care_in_the_United_States">health care in the United
		States</a>, a key campaign promise and a top legislative goal.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-health_reform-303">[303]</a> He proposed an expansion
	of health insurance coverage to cover the uninsured, to cap premium increases, and to allow people to retain their
	coverage when they leave or change jobs. His proposal was to spend $900&nbsp;billion over 10 years and include a
	government insurance plan, also known as the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_health_insurance_option">public option</a>, to compete with the
	corporate insurance sector as a main component to lowering costs and improving quality of health care. It would also
	make it illegal for insurers to drop sick people or deny them coverage for <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pre-existing_condition">pre-existing conditions</a>, and require every
	American to carry health coverage. The plan also includes medical spending cuts and taxes on insurance companies
	that offer expensive plans.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-304">[304]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-305">[305]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/PPACA_Premium_Chart.jpg/300px-PPACA_Premium_Chart.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/PPACA_Premium_Chart.jpg/450px-PPACA_Premium_Chart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/PPACA_Premium_Chart.jpg/600px-PPACA_Premium_Chart.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="300"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Maximum Out-of-Pocket Premium as Percentage of Family Income and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_poverty_level">federal poverty level</a>, under <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act">Patient Protection and
		Affordable Care Act</a>, starting in 2014 (Source: <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congressional_Research_Service">CRS</a>)<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-306">[306]</a></p>

<p>On July 14, 2009, House Democratic leaders introduced a 1,017-page plan for overhauling the U.S. health care system,
	which Obama wanted Congress to approve by the end of 2009.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-health_reform-303">[303]</a> After much public debate
	during the Congressional summer recess of 2009, Obama delivered <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama_speech_to_joint_session_of_Congress,_September_2009">a speech
		to a joint session of Congress</a> on September 9 where he addressed concerns over the proposals.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-307">[307]</a> In March 2009, Obama lifted a ban on
	using federal funds for stem cell research.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-308">[308]</a></p>

<p>On November 7, 2009, a health care bill featuring the public option was passed in the House.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-nyt1-309">[309]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-nyt-310">[310]</a> On December 24, 2009, the Senate
	passed its own bill—without a public option—on a party-line vote of 60–39.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-311">[311]</a> On March 21, 2010, the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act">Patient Protection and
		Affordable Care Act</a> (ACA) passed by the Senate in December was passed in the House by a vote of 219 to
	212.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-312">[312]</a> Obama signed the bill into law on
	March 23, 2010.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-313">[313]</a></p>

<p>The ACA includes <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provisions_of_the_Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act">health-related
		provisions</a>, most of which took effect in 2014, including expanding <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicaid">Medicaid</a> eligibility for people making up to 133%&nbsp;of the
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_poverty_level">federal poverty level</a> (FPL) starting in 2014,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-cnn_ref1-314">[314]</a> subsidizing insurance
	premiums for people making up to 400%&nbsp;of the FPL ($88,000 for family of four in 2010) so their maximum
	"out-of-pocket" payment for annual premiums will be from 2% to 9.5% of income,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-whitehouse-315">[315]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-316">[316]</a> providing incentives for businesses to
	provide health care benefits, prohibiting denial of coverage and denial of claims based on pre-existing conditions,
	establishing <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_insurance_exchange">health insurance exchanges</a>,
	prohibiting annual coverage caps, and support for medical research. According to White House and CBO figures, the
	maximum share of income that enrollees would have to pay would vary depending on their income relative to the
	federal poverty level.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-whitehouse-315">[315]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-cbo_est-317">[317]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Percentage_of_Individuals_in_the_United_States_Without_Health_Insurance%2C_1963-2015.png/220px-Percentage_of_Individuals_in_the_United_States_Without_Health_Insurance%2C_1963-2015.png"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Percentage_of_Individuals_in_the_United_States_Without_Health_Insurance%2C_1963-2015.png/330px-Percentage_of_Individuals_in_the_United_States_Without_Health_Insurance%2C_1963-2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Percentage_of_Individuals_in_the_United_States_Without_Health_Insurance%2C_1963-2015.png/440px-Percentage_of_Individuals_in_the_United_States_Without_Health_Insurance%2C_1963-2015.png 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Percentage of Individuals in the United States without Health Insurance, 1963–2015 (Source: <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JAMA_(journal)">JAMA</a>)<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-318">[318]</a></p>

<p>The costs of these provisions are offset by taxes, fees, and cost-saving measures, such as new Medicare taxes for
	those in high-income <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_bracket">brackets</a>, taxes on <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indoor_tanning">indoor tanning</a>, cuts to the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicare_Advantage">Medicare Advantage</a> program in favor of traditional
	Medicare, and fees on medical devices and pharmaceutical companies;<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-319">[319]</a> there is also a tax penalty for those
	who do not obtain health insurance, unless they are exempt due to low income or other reasons.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-320">[320]</a> In March 2010, the CBO estimated that
	the net effect of both laws will be a reduction in the federal deficit by $143&nbsp;billion over the first decade.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-321">[321]</a></p>

<p>The law faced several legal challenges, primarily based on the argument that an individual mandate requiring
	Americans to buy health insurance was unconstitutional. On June 28, 2012, the Supreme Court ruled by a 5–4 vote in
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Federation_of_Independent_Business_v._Sebelius"><i>National
			Federation of Independent Business v. Sebelius</i></a> that the mandate was constitutional under the U.S.
	Congress's taxing authority.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-WP-uphold-322">[322]</a>
	In <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burwell_v._Hobby_Lobby_Stores,_Inc."><i>Burwell v. Hobby Lobby</i></a> the
	Court ruled that "closely-held" for-profit corporations could be exempt on religious grounds under the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_Freedom_Restoration_Act">Religious Freedom Restoration Act</a>
	from regulations adopted under the ACA that would have required them to pay for insurance that covered certain
	contraceptives. In June 2015, the Court ruled 6–3 in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_v._Burwell"><i>King
			v. Burwell</i></a> that subsidies to help individuals and families purchase health insurance were authorized
	for those doing so on both the federal exchange and state exchanges, not only those purchasing plans "established by
	the State," as the statute reads.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-323">[323]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Energy policy</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_policy_of_the_Obama_administration"><i>Energy
			policy of the Obama administration</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Prior to June 2014, Obama offered substantial support for a broadly-based "All of the above" approach to domestic <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_policy">energy policy</a>, which Obama has maintained since his first
	term and which he last confirmed at his <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_the_Union">State of the
		Union</a> speech in January 2014 to a mixed reception by both parties. In June 2014, Obama made indications that
	his administration would consider a shift towards an energy policy more closely tuned to the manufacturing industry
	and its impact on the domestic economy.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-324">[324]</a>
	Obama's approach of selectively combining regulation and incentive to various issues in the domestic energy policy,
	such as coal mining and oil fracking, has received mixed commentary for not being as responsive to the needs of the
	domestic manufacturing sector as needed, following claims that the domestic manufacturing sector utilizes as much as
	a third of the nation's available energy resources.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-325">[325]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-326">[326]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Gun control</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_policy_of_the_Barack_Obama_administration#Gun_policy"><i>Social
			policy of the Barack Obama administration §&nbsp;Gun policy</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Barack_Obama_visiting_victims_of_2012_Aurora_shooting.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_visiting_victims_of_2012_Aurora_shooting.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Barack_Obama_visiting_victims_of_2012_Aurora_shooting.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_visiting_victims_of_2012_Aurora_shooting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Barack_Obama_visiting_victims_of_2012_Aurora_shooting.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_visiting_victims_of_2012_Aurora_shooting.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama visits an <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Aurora_shooting">Aurora shooting</a> victim at <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Colorado_Hospital">University of Colorado Hospital</a>, 2012.
</p>

<p>On January 16, 2013, one month after the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandy_Hook_Elementary_School_shooting">Sandy Hook Elementary School
		shooting</a>, Obama signed 23 executive orders and outlined a series of sweeping proposals regarding <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gun_politics_in_the_United_States">gun control</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-327">[327]</a> He urged Congress to reintroduce an <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Assault_Weapons_Ban">expired ban</a> on military-style <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assault_weapons">assault weapons</a>, such as those used in several recent
	mass shootings, impose limits on ammunition magazines to 10 rounds, introduce background checks on all gun sales,
	pass a ban on possession and sale of armor-piercing bullets, introduce harsher penalties for gun-traffickers,
	especially unlicensed dealers who buy arms for criminals and approving the appointment of the head of the federal <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bureau_of_Alcohol,_Tobacco,_Firearms_and_Explosives">Bureau of Alcohol,
		Tobacco, Firearms and Explosives</a> for the first time since 2006.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-328">[328]</a> On January 5, 2016, Obama announced
	new executive actions extending background check requirements to more gun sellers.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-329">[329]</a> In a 2016 editorial in the <i>New York
		Times</i>, Obama compared the struggle for what he termed "common-sense gun reform" to <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage">women's suffrage</a> and other <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights_movements">civil rights movements</a> in American history.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-330">[330]</a></p>
<h4><strong>2010 midterm elections</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main articles: </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections"><i>2010 United States
			House of Representatives elections</i></a><i> and </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_United_States_Senate_elections"><i>2010 United States Senate
			elections</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama called the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections">November 2, 2010
		election</a>, where the Democratic Party lost 63 seats in, and control of, the House of Representatives,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-331">[331]</a> "humbling" and a "shellacking."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-332">[332]</a> He said that the results came because
	not enough Americans had felt the effects of the economic recovery.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-333">[333]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Cybersecurity and Internet policy</strong></h4>

<p>On November 10, 2014, President Obama recommended the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a>
	reclassify <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_access">broadband Internet service</a> as a
	telecommunications service in order to preserve <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Net_neutrality">net
		neutrality</a>.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-NYT-20141110-EW-334">[334]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-NYT-20141114-335">[335]</a> On February 12, 2013,
	President Obama signed <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_order_(United_States)">Executive Order</a>
	<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Executive_Order_13636">13636</a>, "Improving Critical Infrastructure
	Cybersecurity."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-336">[336]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Government mass surveillance</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama_on_mass_surveillance"><i>Barack Obama on
			mass surveillance</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>In 2005 and 2006, Obama criticized certain aspects of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patriot_Act">Patriot
		Act</a> for infringing too much on civil liberties and sought as Senator to strengthen civil liberties
	protections.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-337">[337]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-CNN-Snowden-338">[338]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-:0-339">[339]</a> In 2006, he voted to reauthorize a
	revised version of the Patriot Act, saying the law was not ideal but that the revised version had strengthened civil
	liberties.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-:0-339">[339]</a> In 2011, he signed a
	four-year renewal of the Patriot Act.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-340">[340]</a>
	Following the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_surveillance_disclosures_(2013%E2%80%93present)">2013
		global surveillance disclosures</a> by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whistleblower">whistleblower</a>
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Snowden">Edward Snowden</a>, Obama condemned the leak as
	unpatriotic,<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-CNN-Snowden-338">[338]</a> but called for
	increased restrictions on the NSA to address violations of privacy.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-341">[341]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-342">[342]</a> The changes which Obama ordered have
	been described as "modest" however.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-343">[343]</a></p>
<h3><strong>Foreign policy</strong></h3>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_Barack_Obama_administration"><i>Foreign policy of the
			Barack Obama administration</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/P06409PS-0571_%283594694537%29.jpg/220px-P06409PS-0571_%283594694537%29.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/P06409PS-0571_%283594694537%29.jpg/330px-P06409PS-0571_%283594694537%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/P06409PS-0571_%283594694537%29.jpg/440px-P06409PS-0571_%283594694537%29.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>June 4, 2009 − after his speech <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_New_Beginning"><i>A New Beginning</i></a> at
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cairo_University">Cairo University</a>, U.S. President Obama participates in
	a roundtable interview in 2009 with among others <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamal_Khashoggi">Jamal
		Khashoggi</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bambang_Harymurti">Bambang Harymurti</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nahum_Barnea">Nahum Barnea</a>.</p>

<p>In February and March 2009, Vice President Joe Biden and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State">Secretary of State</a> Hillary Clinton
	made separate overseas trips to announce a "new era" in U.S. foreign relations with Russia and Europe, using the
	terms "break" and "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_reset">reset</a>" to signal major changes from the
	policies of the preceding administration.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-preceding_administration-344">[344]</a> Obama
	attempted to reach out to Arab leaders by granting his first interview to an Arab satellite TV network, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Arabiya">Al Arabiya</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-345">[345]</a></p>

<p>On March 19, Obama continued his outreach to the Muslim world, releasing a New Year's video message to the people and
	government of Iran.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-346">[346]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-347">[347]</a> In April, Obama gave a speech in <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara">Ankara</a>, Turkey, which was well received by many Arab
	governments.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-348">[348]</a> On June 4, 2009, Obama
	delivered a speech at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cairo_University">Cairo University</a> in Egypt calling
	for "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_New_Beginning">A New Beginning</a>" in relations between the Islamic
	world and the United States and promoting Middle East peace.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-middleeast-349">[349]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Barack_Obama_foreign_trips.svg/220px-Barack_Obama_foreign_trips.svg.png"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Barack_Obama_foreign_trips.svg/330px-Barack_Obama_foreign_trips.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Barack_Obama_foreign_trips.svg/440px-Barack_Obama_foreign_trips.svg.png 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_international_presidential_trips_made_by_Barack_Obama">International
		trips</a> made by President Barack Obama during his terms in office</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Merkel_an_Obama_Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg/220px-Merkel_an_Obama_Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Merkel_an_Obama_Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg/330px-Merkel_an_Obama_Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Merkel_an_Obama_Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg/440px-Merkel_an_Obama_Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama with German Chancellor <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angela_Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> in 2011</p>

<p>On June 26, 2009, Obama responded to the Iranian government's actions towards protesters following <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_Iranian_presidential_election">Iran's 2009 presidential election</a> by
	saying: "The violence perpetrated against them is outrageous. We see it and we condemn it."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-350">[350]</a> While in Moscow on July 7, he
	responded to Vice President Biden's comment on a possible Israeli military strike on Iran by saying: "We have said
	directly to the Israelis that it is important to try and resolve this in an international setting in a way that does
	not create major conflict in the Middle East."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-351">[351]</a></p>

<p>On September 24, 2009, Obama became the first sitting U.S. President to <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council">preside</a> over a meeting
	of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council">United Nations Security
		Council</a>.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-352">[352]</a></p>

<p>In March 2010, Obama took a public stance against plans by the government of Israeli Prime Minister <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a> to continue building Jewish
	housing projects in predominantly Arab neighborhoods of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Jerusalem">East
		Jerusalem</a>.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-353">[353]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-354">[354]</a> During the same month, an agreement
	was reached with the administration of Russian President <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> to replace the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/START_I">1991 Strategic Arms Reduction Treaty</a> with a new pact reducing
	the number of long-range nuclear weapons in the arsenals of both countries by about a third.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-355">[355]</a> Obama and Medvedev signed the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_START">New START</a> treaty in April 2010, and the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate">U.S. Senate</a> ratified it in December 2010.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-356">[356]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Barack_Obama_and_Matteo_Renzi_October_2016%2C_1.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_and_Matteo_Renzi_October_2016%2C_1.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Barack_Obama_and_Matteo_Renzi_October_2016%2C_1.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_and_Matteo_Renzi_October_2016%2C_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Barack_Obama_and_Matteo_Renzi_October_2016%2C_1.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_and_Matteo_Renzi_October_2016%2C_1.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama meets with Italian Prime Minister <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matteo_Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a> at the
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House">White House</a>, October 2016.</p>

<p>In December 2011, Obama instructed agencies to consider <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_rights_by_country_or_territory">LGBT rights</a> when issuing financial
	aid to foreign countries.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-357">[357]</a> In August
	2013, he criticized Russia's law that discriminates against gays,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-LAT80713-358">[358]</a> but he stopped short of
	advocating a boycott of the upcoming <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics">2014 Winter
		Olympics</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sochi">Sochi</a>, Russia.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Huffpo80913-359">[359]</a></p>

<p>In December 2014, Obama announced that he intended to <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Cuban_Thaw">normalize relationships</a> between <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93United_States_relations">Cuba and the United States</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-360">[360]</a> The countries' respective "interests
	sections" in one another's capitals were upgraded to embassies on July 20, 2015.</p>

<p>In March 2015, Obama declared that he had authorized U.S. forces to provide logistical and intelligence support to
	the Saudis in their <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen">military
		intervention in Yemen</a>, establishing a "Joint Planning Cell" with Saudi Arabia.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-361">[361]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-362">[362]</a> In 2016, the Obama administration
	proposed a series of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia%E2%80%93United_States_relations">arms deals
		with Saudi Arabia</a> worth $115 billion.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-363">[363]</a> Obama halted the sale of guided
	munition technology to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> after Saudi warplanes
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_Sana%27a_funeral_airstrike">targeted a funeral</a> in Yemen's capital
	Sanaa, killing more than 140 people.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-364">[364]</a></p>

<p>Before leaving office, Obama said German Chancellor <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angela_Merkel">Angela
		Merkel</a> had been his "closest international partner" throughout his tenure as president.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-thelocal2016-365">[365]</a></p>
<h4><strong>War in Iraq</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main articles: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq_War"><i>Iraq War</i></a><i> and </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American-led_intervention_in_Iraq_(2014%E2%80%93present)"><i>American-led
			intervention in Iraq (2014–present)</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>On February 27, 2009, Obama announced that combat operations in Iraq would end within 18 months. His remarks were
	made to a group of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps">Marines</a> preparing for
	deployment to Afghanistan. Obama said, "Let me say this as plainly as I can: by August 31, 2010, our combat mission
	in Iraq will end."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-366">[366]</a> The Obama
	administration scheduled the withdrawal of combat troops to be completed by August 2010, decreasing troop's levels
	from 142,000 while leaving a transitional force of about 50,000 in Iraq until the end of 2011. On August 19, 2010,
	the last U.S. combat brigade exited Iraq. Remaining troops transitioned from combat operations to <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counter-terrorism">counter-terrorism</a> and the training, equipping, and
	advising of Iraqi security forces.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-367">[367]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-368">[368]</a> On August 31, 2010, Obama announced
	that the United States combat mission in Iraq was over.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-369">[369]</a> On October 21, 2011 President Obama
	announced that all U.S. troops would leave Iraq in time to be "home for the holidays."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-370">[370]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg/220px-David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg"
		alt="US President Barack Obama and British Prime Minister David Cameron trade bottles of beer to settle a bet they made on the U.S. vs. England World Cup Soccer game (which ended in a tie), during a bilateral meeting at the G20 Summit in Toronto, Canada, Saturday, June 26, 2010."
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg/330px-David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg/440px-David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg 2x"
