		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Meeting with UK Prime Minister <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Cameron">David Cameron</a> during the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_G20_Toronto_summit">2010 G20 Toronto summit</a></p>

<p>In June 2014, following the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Iraq_offensive_(June_2014)#Fall_of_Mosul_and_push_into_Kirkuk">capture
		of Mosul</a> by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant">ISIS</a>, Obama
	sent 275 troops to provide support and security for U.S. personnel and the U.S. Embassy in Baghdad. ISIS continued
	to gain ground and to commit <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant#Human_rights_abuse_and_war_crime_findings">widespread
		massacres and ethnic cleansing</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-371">[371]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-372">[372]</a></p>

<p>In August 2014, during the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinjar_massacre">Sinjar massacre</a>, Obama ordered
	a <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American-led_intervention_in_Iraq_(2014%E2%80%93present)#United_States_airstrikes">campaign
		of U.S. airstrikes against ISIS</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-def31-10-14-373">[373]</a></p>

<p>By the end of 2014, 3,100 American ground troops were committed to the conflict<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-374">[374]</a> and 16,000 sorties were flown over the
	battlefield, primarily by U.S. Air Force and Navy pilots.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-375">[375]</a></p>

<p>In early 2015, with the addition of the "Panther Brigade" of the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/82nd_Airborne_Division">82nd Airborne Division</a> the number of U.S. ground
	troops in Iraq surged to 4,400,<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-376">[376]</a> and by
	July American-led coalition air forces counted 44,000 sorties over the battlefield.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-377">[377]</a></p>
<h4><strong>War in Afghanistan</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)"><i>War in
			Afghanistan (2001–present)</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Early in his presidency, Obama moved to bolster U.S. troop strength in Afghanistan.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-autogenerated1-378">[378]</a> He announced an
	increase in U.S. troop levels to 17,000 military personnel in February 2009 to "stabilize a deteriorating situation
	in Afghanistan," an area he said had not received the "strategic attention, direction and resources it urgently
	requires."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-379">[379]</a> He replaced the military
	commander in Afghanistan, General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_D._McKiernan">David D. McKiernan</a>,
	with former <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Forces_(United_States_Army)">Special Forces</a> commander
	Lt. Gen. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanley_A._McChrystal">Stanley A. McChrystal</a> in May 2009,
	indicating that McChrystal's Special Forces experience would facilitate the use of counterinsurgency tactics in the
	war.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-counterinsurgency_tactics-380">[380]</a> On
	December 1, 2009, Obama announced the deployment of an additional 30,000 military personnel to Afghanistan and
	proposed to begin troop withdrawals 18 months from that date;<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-381">[381]</a> this took place in July 2011. <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Petraeus">David Petraeus</a> replaced McChrystal in June 2010, after
	McChrystal's staff criticized White House personnel in a magazine article.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-382">[382]</a> In February 2013, Obama said the U.S.
	military would reduce the troop level in Afghanistan from 68,000 to 34,000 U.S. troops by February 2014.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-383">[383]</a></p>

<p>In October 2015, the White House announced a plan to keep U.S. Forces in Afghanistan indefinitely in light of the
	deteriorating security situation.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-384">[384]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Israel</strong></h4>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Barack_Obama_welcomes_Shimon_Peres_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_welcomes_Shimon_Peres_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg"
		alt="President Barack Obama, at left, shakes hands with Israeli President Shimon Peres, at right, in the Oval Office on Tuesday, May 5, 2009. Standing at right looking on is U.S. Vice President Joe Biden."
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Barack_Obama_welcomes_Shimon_Peres_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_welcomes_Shimon_Peres_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Barack_Obama_welcomes_Shimon_Peres_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_welcomes_Shimon_Peres_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama meeting with Israeli President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shimon_Peres">Shimon Peres</a> in the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oval_Office">Oval Office</a>, May 2009</p>

<p>In 2011, the United States vetoed a Security Council resolution condemning <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_settlement">Israeli settlements</a>, with the United States being
	the only nation to do so.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-385">[385]</a> Obama supports
	the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Two-state_solution">two-state solution</a> to the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict">Arab–Israeli conflict</a> based on the 1967
	borders with land swaps.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-386">[386]</a></p>

<p>In June 2011, Obama said the bond between the United States and Israel is "unbreakable."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-387">[387]</a> During the initial years of the Obama
	administration, the U.S. increased military cooperation with Israel, including increased military aid,
	re-establishment of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Political_Military_Group">U.S.-Israeli Joint
		Political Military Group</a> and the Defense Policy Advisory Group, and an increase in visits among high-level
	military officials of both countries.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-388">[388]</a>
	The Obama administration asked Congress to allocate money toward funding the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Dome">Iron Dome</a> program in response to the waves of <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel">Palestinian rocket attacks on
		Israel</a>.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-389">[389]</a></p>

<p>In 2013, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeffrey_Goldberg">Jeffrey Goldberg</a> reported that, in Obama's
	view, "with each new settlement announcement, Netanyahu is moving his country down a path toward near-total
	isolation."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Bloomberg-390">[390]</a> In 2014, Obama
	likened the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionism">Zionist movement</a> to the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_Rights_Movement">Civil Rights Movement</a> in the United States. He
	said both movements seek to bring justice and equal rights to historically persecuted peoples. He explained, "To me,
	being pro-Israel and pro-Jewish is part and parcel with the values that I've been fighting for since I was
	politically conscious and started getting involved in politics."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-391">[391]</a> Obama expressed support for Israel's
	right to defend itself during the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict">2014
		Israel–Gaza conflict</a>.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-392">[392]</a> In 2015,
	Obama was harshly criticized by Israel for advocating and signing the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action">Iran Nuclear Deal</a>; Israeli Prime
	Minister <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>, who had advocated the
	U.S. congress to oppose it, said the deal was "dangerous" and "bad."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-393">[393]</a></p>

<p>On December 23, 2016, under the Obama Administration, the United States abstained from <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_2334">United Nations Security
		Council Resolution 2334</a>, which condemned <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_settlement">Israeli
		settlement building</a> in the occupied <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_territories">Palestinian territories</a> as a violation of
	international law, effectively allowing it to pass.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-394">[394]</a> Netanyahu strongly criticized the
	Obama Administration's actions,<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-395">[395]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-396">[396]</a> and the Israeli government withdrew
	its annual dues from the organization, which totaled $6 million, on January 6, 2017.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-397">[397]</a> On January 5, 2017, the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives">United States House of
		Representatives</a> voted 342–80 to condemn the UN Resolution.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-398">[398]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-399">[399]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Libya</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya"><i>2011 military
			intervention in Libya</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_04.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_04.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_04.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_04.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_04.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>President Obama meets with Russian President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin">Vladimir
		Putin</a> to discuss Syria and ISIS, September 29, 2015.</p>

<p>In February 2011, protests in Libya began against long-time dictator <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a> as part of the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Spring">Arab Spring</a>. They soon turned violent. In March, as forces
	loyal to Gaddafi advanced on rebels across Libya, calls for a no-fly zone came from around the world, including
	Europe, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League">Arab League</a>, and a resolution<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-400">[400]</a> passed unanimously by the U.S.
	Senate.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-401">[401]</a> In response to the unanimous
	passage of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1973">United Nations
		Security Council Resolution 1973</a> on March 17, Gaddafi—who had previously vowed to "show no mercy" to the
	rebels of Benghazi<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-402">[402]</a>—announced an
	immediate cessation of military activities,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-403">[403]</a> yet reports came in that his forces
	continued shelling <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Misrata">Misrata</a>. The next day, on Obama's orders, the
	U.S. military took part in air strikes to destroy the Libyan government's air defense capabilities to protect
	civilians and enforce a no-fly-zone,<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-404">[404]</a>
	including the use of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomahawk_(missile)">Tomahawk missiles</a>, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northrop_Grumman_B-2_Spirit">B-2 Spirits</a>, and fighter jets.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-405">[405]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-406">[406]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-407">[407]</a> Six days later, on March 25, by
	unanimous vote of all its 28 members, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO">NATO</a> took over leadership of
	the effort, dubbed <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Unified_Protector">Operation Unified
		Protector</a>.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-NATOPressRelease-408">[408]</a> Some
	Representatives<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-LibyaOffensive-409">[409]</a>
	questioned whether Obama had the constitutional authority to order military action in addition to questioning its
	cost, structure and aftermath.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-410">[410]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-411">[411]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Syrian Civil War</strong></h4>

<p><i>See also: </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_involvement_in_the_Syrian_Civil_War#United_States"><i>Foreign
			involvement in the Syrian Civil War §&nbsp;United States</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>On August 18, 2011, several months after the start of the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War">Syrian Civil War</a>, Obama issued a written statement
	that said: "The time has come for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad">President Assad</a> to
	step aside."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-mustgo-412">[412]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-whstatem-413">[413]</a> This stance was reaffirmed in
	November 2015.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-414">[414]</a> In 2012, Obama authorized
	multiple <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timber_Sycamore">programs run by the CIA</a> and the Pentagon to
	train anti-Assad rebels.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-415">[415]</a> The
	Pentagon-run program was later found to have failed and was formally abandoned in October 2015.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-416">[416]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-417">[417]</a></p>

<p>In the wake of a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghouta_chemical_attack">chemical weapons attack</a> in Syria,
	<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Government_Assessment_of_the_Syrian_Government%27s_Use_of_Chemical_Weapons_on_August_21,_2013">formally
		blamed</a> by the Obama administration on the Assad government, Obama chose not to enforce the "red line" he had
	pledged<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-redline-418">[418]</a> and, rather than
	authorize the promised military action against Assad, went along with the Russia-brokered deal that led to Assad <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Destruction_of_Syria%27s_chemical_weapons">giving up chemical weapons</a>;
	however attacks with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorine_gas">chlorine gas</a> continued.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-419">[419]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-420">[420]</a> In 2014, Obama authorized an <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_intervention_against_ISIL">air campaign aimed primarily at
		ISIL</a>, but repeatedly promised the U.S. would not deploy ground troops in Syria.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-421">[421]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-422">[422]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Death of Osama bin Laden</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_of_Osama_bin_Laden"><i>Death of Osama bin
			Laden</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/President_Obama_on_Death_of_Osama_bin_Laden.ogv/220px--President_Obama_on_Death_of_Osama_bin_Laden.ogv.jpg"
		alt="File:President Obama on Death of Osama bin Laden.ogv"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>President Obama's address (9:28)<br><i>Also available:</i> <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:050111_Osama_Bin_Laden_Death_Statement_audioonly.ogg">Audio only</a>;
	<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Remarks_by_the_President_on_Osama_bin_Laden">Full text</a>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/11px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png"
		alt="Wikisource has information on &quot;Remarks by the President on Osama bin Laden&quot;"
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/17px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/22px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="11"></figure>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Obama_and_Biden_await_updates_on_bin_Laden.jpg/220px-Obama_and_Biden_await_updates_on_bin_Laden.jpg"
		alt="President Barack Obama and Vice President Joe Biden, along with members of the national security team, receive an update on Operation Neptune's Spear, a mission against Osama bin Laden, in one of the conference rooms of the Situation Room of the White House, on May 1, 2011. They are watching live feed from drones operating over the bin Laden complex."
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Obama_and_Biden_await_updates_on_bin_Laden.jpg/330px-Obama_and_Biden_await_updates_on_bin_Laden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Obama_and_Biden_await_updates_on_bin_Laden.jpg/440px-Obama_and_Biden_await_updates_on_bin_Laden.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama and members of the national security team receive an update on <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Neptune%27s_Spear">Operation Neptune's Spear</a> in the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Situation_Room">White House Situation Room</a>, May 1, 2011. See
	also: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Situation_Room_(photograph)"><i>Situation Room</i></a></p>

<p>Starting with information received from Central Intelligence Agency operatives in July 2010, the CIA developed
	intelligence over the next several months that determined what they believed to be the hideout of <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden">Osama bin Laden</a>. He was living in seclusion in <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden%27s_compound_in_Abbottabad">a large compound</a> in <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbottabad">Abbottabad</a>, Pakistan, a suburban area 35 miles (56&nbsp;km)
	from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamabad">Islamabad</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-NYT-clues-423">[423]</a> CIA head <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Panetta">Leon Panetta</a> reported this intelligence to President Obama
	in March 2011.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-NYT-clues-423">[423]</a> Meeting with
	his national security advisers over the course of the next six weeks, Obama rejected a plan to bomb the compound,
	and authorized a "surgical raid" to be conducted by <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Navy_SEALs">United States Navy SEALs</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-NYT-clues-423">[423]</a> The operation took place on
	May 1, 2011, and resulted in the shooting death of bin Laden and the seizure of papers, computer drives and disks
	from the compound.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-WP-binLaden-424">[424]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-ND-binLaden-425">[425]</a> DNA testing was one of
	five methods used to positively identify bin Laden's corpse,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-ABC-binLaden-426">[426]</a> which was buried at sea
	several hours later.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-NYT-ObamaAnnounce-427">[427]</a>
	Within minutes of the President's announcement from Washington, DC, late in the evening on May 1, there were
	spontaneous celebrations around the country as crowds gathered outside the White House, and at New York City's <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Center_site">Ground Zero</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Square">Times Square</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-WP-binLaden-424">[424]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Guard-ObamaAnnounce-428">[428]</a> <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reactions_to_the_death_of_Osama_bin_Laden">Reaction to the announcement</a>
	was positive across party lines, including from former presidents Bill Clinton and George W. Bush.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Bloom-binLaden-429">[429]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Iran nuclear talks</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action"><i>Joint
			Comprehensive Plan of Action</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Barack_Obama_talks_with_Benjamin_Netanyahu_%288637772147%29.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_talks_with_Benjamin_Netanyahu_%288637772147%29.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Barack_Obama_talks_with_Benjamin_Netanyahu_%288637772147%29.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_talks_with_Benjamin_Netanyahu_%288637772147%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Barack_Obama_talks_with_Benjamin_Netanyahu_%288637772147%29.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_talks_with_Benjamin_Netanyahu_%288637772147%29.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama talks with Benjamin Netanyahu, March 2013.</p>

<p>In November 2013, the Obama administration opened <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negotiations_leading_to_the_Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action">negotiations</a>
	with Iran to prevent it from acquiring <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon">nuclear weapons</a>,
	which included an <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Plan_of_Action">interim agreement</a>. Negotiations
	took two years with numerous delays, with a deal being announced July 14, 2015. The deal, titled the "<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action">Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action</a>,"
	saw the removal of sanctions in exchange for measures that would prevent Iran from producing nuclear weapons. While
	Obama hailed the agreement as being a step towards a more hopeful world, the deal drew strong criticism from
	Republican and conservative quarters, and from Israeli prime minister <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-430">[430]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-431">[431]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-432">[432]</a> In addition, the transfer of $1.7
	billion in cash to Iran shortly after the deal was announced was criticized by the republican party. The Obama
	administration said that the payment in cash was because of the "effectiveness of U.S. and international
	sanctions."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-433">[433]</a> In order to advance the
	deal, the Obama administration shielded <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> from the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration">Drug Enforcement Administration</a>'s <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Project_Cassandra">Project Cassandra</a> investigation regarding drug
	smuggling and from the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency">Central Intelligence
		Agency</a>.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-434">[434]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-435">[435]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Relations with Cuba</strong></h4>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Cuban_Thaw"><i>United States–Cuban
			Thaw</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Handshake_between_the_President_and_Cuban_President_Ra%C3%BAl_Castro.jpg/220px-Handshake_between_the_President_and_Cuban_President_Ra%C3%BAl_Castro.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Handshake_between_the_President_and_Cuban_President_Ra%C3%BAl_Castro.jpg/330px-Handshake_between_the_President_and_Cuban_President_Ra%C3%BAl_Castro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Handshake_between_the_President_and_Cuban_President_Ra%C3%BAl_Castro.jpg/440px-Handshake_between_the_President_and_Cuban_President_Ra%C3%BAl_Castro.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>President Obama meeting with Cuban President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Castro">Raúl Castro</a>
	in Panama, April 2015</p>

<p>Since the spring of 2013, secret meetings were conducted between the United States and Cuba in the neutral locations
	of Canada and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vatican_City">Vatican City</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-436">[436]</a> The Vatican first became involved in
	2013 when <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Francis">Pope Francis</a> advised the U.S. and Cuba to <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoner_exchange">exchange prisoners</a> as a gesture of goodwill.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-437">[437]</a> On December 10, 2013, Cuban President
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Castro">Raúl Castro</a>, in a significant public moment, greeted
	and shook hands with Obama at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_of_Nelson_Mandela">Nelson Mandela
		memorial service</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-438">[438]</a></p>

<p>In December 2014, after the secret meetings, it was announced that Obama, with <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Francis">Pope Francis</a> as an intermediary, had negotiated a
	restoration of relations with Cuba, after nearly sixty years of détente.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-439">[439]</a> Popularly dubbed the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_Thaw">Cuban Thaw</a>, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_Republic"><i>The New Republic</i></a> deemed the Cuban Thaw to be
	"Obama's finest foreign policy achievement."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-440">[440]</a> On July 1, 2015, President Barack
	Obama announced that formal diplomatic relations between Cuba and the United States would resume, and embassies
	would be opened in Washington and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Havana">Havana</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-441">[441]</a> The countries' respective "interests
	sections" in one another's capitals were upgraded to embassies on July 20 and August 13, 2015, respectively.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-442">[442]</a></p>

<p>Obama visited Havana, Cuba for two days in March 2016, becoming the first sitting U.S. President to arrive since <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calvin_Coolidge">Calvin Coolidge</a> in 1928.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-443">[443]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Africa</strong></h4>

<p>Obama spoke in front of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_Union">African Union</a> in <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Addis_Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, Ethiopia, on July 29, 2015, the first sitting
	U.S. president to do so. He gave a speech encouraging the world to increase economic ties via investments and trade
	with the continent, and lauded the progress made in <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education_in_Africa">education</a>, infrastructure, and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_Africa">economy</a>. He also criticized the lack of democracy and
	leaders who refuse to step aside, discrimination against minorities (<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT">LGBT</a> people, religious groups and ethnicities), and corruption. He
	suggested an intensified <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratization">democratization</a> and free trade,
	to significantly improve the quality of life for Africans.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-444">[444]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-445">[445]</a> During his July 2015 trip, Obama also
	was the first U.S. president ever to <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_presidential_visits_to_Sub-Saharan_Africa">visit</a> Kenya,
	which is the homeland of his father.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-446">[446]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Hiroshima speech</strong></h4>

<p>On May 27, 2016, Obama became the first sitting American president to visit <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hiroshima">Hiroshima</a>, Japan, 71 years after the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki">U.S. atomic bombing of
		Hiroshima</a> that ended <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II">World War II</a>. Accompanied by
	Japanese Prime Minister <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shinz%C5%8D_Abe">Shinzō Abe</a>, Obama paid tribute
	to the victims of the bombing at the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hiroshima_Peace_Memorial_Museum">Hiroshima Peace Memorial Museum</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-447">[447]</a></p>
<h4><strong>Russia</strong></h4>

<p><i>See also: </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia%E2%80%93United_States_relations#Obama's_tenure_(2009%E2%80%9317)"><i>Russia–United
			States relations §&nbsp;Obama's tenure (2009–17)</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_01.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_01.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_01.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_01.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Barack_Obama_%282015-09-29%29_01.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama meets Russian President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> in September
	2015.</p>

<p>After <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation">Russia's invasion of
		Crimea</a> in 2014, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_military_intervention_in_Syria">military
		intervention</a> in Syria in 2015, and the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_United_States_election_interference_by_Russia">interference</a> in the
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election">2016 U.S. presidential
		election</a>,<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-ftelect-448">[448]</a> Obama's Russia
	policy was widely seen as a failure.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-friedmnyt-449">[449]</a> <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Robertson,_Baron_Robertson_of_Port_Ellen">George Robertson</a>, a
	former UK defense secretary and NATO secretary-general, said Obama had "allowed Putin to jump back on the world
	stage and test the resolve of the West," adding that the legacy of this disaster would last.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-obexit-450">[450]</a></p>
<h3><strong>Cultural and political image</strong></h3>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_image_of_Barack_Obama"><i>Public image of Barack
			Obama</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><i>See also: </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_reactions_to_the_2008_United_States_presidential_election"><i>International
			reactions to the 2008 United States presidential election</i></a><i> and </i><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_reactions_to_the_2012_United_States_presidential_election"><i>International
			reactions to the 2012 United States presidential election</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama's family history, upbringing, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivy_League">Ivy League</a> education
	differ markedly from those of African-American politicians who launched their careers in the 1960s through
	participation in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights_movement">civil rights movement</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-451">[451]</a> Expressing puzzlement over questions
	about whether he is "black enough," Obama told an August 2007 meeting of the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Association_of_Black_Journalists">National Association of Black
		Journalists</a> that "we're still locked in this notion that if you appeal to white folks then there must be
	something wrong."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-452">[452]</a> Obama acknowledged his
	youthful image in an October 2007 campaign speech, saying: "I wouldn't be here if, time and again, the torch had not
	been passed to a new generation."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-453">[453]</a></p>

<p>Obama is frequently referred to as an exceptional orator.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-exceptional_orator-454">[454]</a> During his
	pre-inauguration transition period and continuing into his presidency, Obama delivered a series of weekly Internet
	video addresses.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-455">[455]</a> In his speeches as
	president, Obama did not make more overt references to race relations than his predecessors,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-456">[456]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-457">[457]</a> but according to one study, he
	implemented stronger policy action on behalf of African-Americans than any president since the Nixon era.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-458">[458]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Gallup_Poll-Approval_Rating-Barack_Obama.svg/220px-Gallup_Poll-Approval_Rating-Barack_Obama.svg.png"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Gallup_Poll-Approval_Rating-Barack_Obama.svg/330px-Gallup_Poll-Approval_Rating-Barack_Obama.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Gallup_Poll-Approval_Rating-Barack_Obama.svg/440px-Gallup_Poll-Approval_Rating-Barack_Obama.svg.png 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Presidential approval ratings</p>

<p>According to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallup_Organization">Gallup Organization</a>, Obama began his
	presidency with a 68% approval rating<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-459">[459]</a>
	before gradually declining for the rest of the year, and eventually bottoming out at 41% in August 2010,<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-460">[460]</a> a trend similar to <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>'s and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>'s first years in office.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-461">[461]</a> He experienced a small poll bounce
	shortly after the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_of_Osama_bin_Laden">death of Osama bin Laden</a> on
	May 2, 2011. This bounce lasted until around June 2011, when his approval numbers dropped back to where they were
	previously.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-462">[462]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-463">[463]</a> His approval ratings rebounded around
	the same time as his reelection in 2012, with polls showing an average job approval of 52% shortly after his second
	inauguration.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-464">[464]</a> Despite approval ratings
	dropping to 39% in late-2013 due to the ACA roll-out, they climbed to 50% in January 2015 according to Gallup.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-465">[465]</a></p>

<p>Polls showed strong support for Obama in other countries both before and during his presidency.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-466">[466]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-467">[467]</a> In a February 2009 poll conducted in
	Western Europe and the U.S. by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harris_Insights_%26_Analytics">Harris
		Interactive</a> for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France_24">France 24</a> and the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Herald_Tribune"><i>International Herald Tribune</i></a>, Obama
	was rated as the most respected world leader, as well as the most powerful.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-468">[468]</a> In a similar poll conducted by Harris
	in May 2009, Obama was rated as the most popular world leader, as well as the one figure most people would pin their
	hopes on for pulling the world out of the economic downturn.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-469">[469]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-470">[470]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/G8_leaders_watching_football.jpg/220px-G8_leaders_watching_football.jpg"
		alt="Prime Minister David Cameron of the United Kingdom, President Barack Obama, Chancellor Angela Merkel of Germany, José Manuel Barroso, President of the European Commission, President François Hollande of France and others react emotionally while watching the overtime shootout of the Chelsea vs. Bayern Munich Champions League final, in the Laurel Cabin conference room during the G8 Summit at Camp David, Maryland, May 19, 2012. Cameron raises his arms triumphantly as the Chelsea team wins their first Champions League title in the overtime shootout."
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/G8_leaders_watching_football.jpg/330px-G8_leaders_watching_football.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/G8_leaders_watching_football.jpg/440px-G8_leaders_watching_football.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>G8 leaders watching the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_UEFA_Champions_League_Final">2012 UEFA Champions
		League Final</a></p>

<p>Obama won <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Spoken_Word_Album">Best Spoken Word Album</a>
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grammy_Award">Grammy Awards</a> for abridged <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Audiobook">audiobook</a> versions of <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dreams_from_My_Father"><i>Dreams from My Father</i></a> in February 2006 and
	for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Audacity_of_Hope"><i>The Audacity of Hope</i></a> in February 2008.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-471">[471]</a> His <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama_presidential_primary_campaign,_2008#New_Hampshire">concession
		speech</a> after the New Hampshire primary was set to music by independent artists as the music video "<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yes_We_Can_(will.i.am_song)">Yes We Can</a>," which was viewed
	10&nbsp;million times on YouTube in its first month<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-472">[472]</a> and received a <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award">Daytime Emmy Award</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-473">[473]</a> In December 2008 and in 2012, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_(magazine)"><i>Time</i></a> magazine named Obama as its <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_Person_of_the_Year">Person of the Year</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-474">[474]</a> The 2008 awarding was for his historic
	candidacy and election, which <i>Time</i> described as "the steady march of seemingly impossible accomplishments."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-475">[475]</a> On May 25, 2011, Obama became the
	first President of the United States to address both houses of the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom">UK Parliament</a> in <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Westminster_Hall">Westminster Hall</a>, London. This was only the fifth
	occurrence since the start of the 20th century of a head of state's being extended this invitation, following <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> in 1960, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nelson_Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> in 1996, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> in 2002 and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> in 2010.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-476">[476]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-477">[477]</a></p>

<p>On October 9, 2009, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norwegian_Nobel_Committee">Norwegian Nobel
		Committee</a> announced that Obama had won the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_Nobel_Peace_Prize">2009 Nobel Peace Prize</a> "for his extraordinary
	efforts to strengthen international diplomacy and cooperation between peoples."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-nobel_peace_prize-478">[478]</a> Obama accepted this
	award in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oslo">Oslo</a>, Norway on December 10, 2009, with "deep gratitude
	and great humility."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-CNN:_Obama_acceptance_transcript-479">[479]</a> The
	award drew a mixture of praise and criticism from world leaders and media figures.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-480">[480]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-481">[481]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-482">[482]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-483">[483]</a> Obama's peace prize was called a
	"stunning surprise" by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times"><i>The New York Times</i></a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-484">[484]</a> Obama is the fourth U.S. president to
	be awarded the Nobel Peace Prize and the third to become a Nobel laureate while in office.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-485">[485]</a> Obama's Nobel Prize has been viewed
	skeptically in subsequent years, especially after the director of the Nobel Institute, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geir_Lundestad">Geir Lundestad</a>, said Obama's Peace Prize did not have
	the desired effect.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-486">[486]</a></p>
<h2>Post-presidency (2017–present)</h2>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/58th_Presidential_Inaugural_Ceremony_170120-D-BP749-1327.jpg/220px-58th_Presidential_Inaugural_Ceremony_170120-D-BP749-1327.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/58th_Presidential_Inaugural_Ceremony_170120-D-BP749-1327.jpg/330px-58th_Presidential_Inaugural_Ceremony_170120-D-BP749-1327.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/58th_Presidential_Inaugural_Ceremony_170120-D-BP749-1327.jpg/440px-58th_Presidential_Inaugural_Ceremony_170120-D-BP749-1327.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama, with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden">Joe Biden</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump">Donald Trump</a> at the latter's <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inauguration_of_Donald_Trump">inauguration</a> on January 20, 2017</p>

<p>Obama's presidency ended at noon on January 20, 2017, immediately following the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inauguration_of_Donald_Trump">inauguration</a> of his Republican successor,
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump">Donald Trump</a>. After the inauguration, Obama lifted off on
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_One">Executive One</a>, circled the White House, and flew to <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Base_Andrews">Joint Base Andrews</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-487">[487]</a> The family currently rents a house in
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kalorama,_Washington,_D.C.">Kalorama, Washington, D.C.</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-488">[488]</a></p>

<p>On March 2, 2017, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Presidential_Library_and_Museum">John F.
		Kennedy Presidential Library and Museum</a> awarded the annual <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Profile_in_Courage_Award">Profile in Courage Award</a> to Obama "for his
	enduring commitment to democratic ideals and elevating the standard of political courage."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-489">[489]</a> In his first public appearance out of
	office, Obama appeared at a seminar at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Chicago">University
		of Chicago</a> on April 24. The seminar was aimed at the engagement with a new generation as well as an appeal
	for their participation in politics.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-490">[490]</a> On
	May 4, three days ahead of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_French_presidential_election">French
		presidential election</a>, Obama publicly endorsed <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmanuel_Macron">Emmanuel Macron</a>: "He appeals to people's hopes and not
	their fears, and I enjoyed speaking to Emmanuel recently to hear about his independent movement and his vision for
	the future of France."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-491">[491]</a> Macron went on to
	win the election.</p>

<p>While in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin">Berlin</a> on May 25, Obama made a joint public appearance
	with Chancellor <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angela_Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> where he stressed inclusion
	and for leaders to question themselves, Obama having been formally invited to Berlin while still in office as part
	of an effort to boost Merkel's re-election campaign.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-492">[492]</a> Obama traveled to <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kensington_Palace">Kensington Palace</a> in England and met with <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_Harry">Prince Harry</a> on May 27, 2017; Obama tweeted afterward that
	the two discussed their foundations and offering condolences in the wake of the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_Manchester_Arena_bombing">Manchester Arena bombing</a> that occurred
	five days prior.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-493">[493]</a></p>

<p>After President Trump announced his withdrawal of the United States from the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> on June 1, Obama released a statement
	disagreeing with the choice: "But even in the absence of American leadership; even as this administration joins a
	small handful of nations that reject the future; I'm confident that our states, cities, and businesses will step up
	and do even more to lead the way, and help protect for future generations the one planet we've got."<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-494">[494]</a></p>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Obama_Macri_October_2017.jpg/220px-Obama_Macri_October_2017.jpg"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Obama_Macri_October_2017.jpg/330px-Obama_Macri_October_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Obama_Macri_October_2017.jpg/440px-Obama_Macri_October_2017.jpg 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="220"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Obama playing golf with the President of Argentina <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mauricio_Macri">Mauricio
		Macri</a>, October 2017</p>

<p>After Senate Republicans revealed the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Better_Care_Reconciliation_Act_of_2017">Better Care Reconciliation Act of
		2017</a>, their discussion draft of a health care bill to replace the Affordable Care Act, on June 22, Obama
	released a Facebook post calling the bill "a massive transfer of wealth from middle-class and poor families to the
	richest people in America."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-495">[495]</a> On September
	19, while delivering the keynote address at Goalkeepers, Obama admitted his frustration with Republicans backing "a
	bill that will raise costs, reduce coverage, and roll back protections for older Americans and people with
	pre-existing conditions."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-496">[496]</a></p>

<p>After Attorney General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeff_Sessions">Jeff Sessions</a> announced the
	termination of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deferred_Action_for_Childhood_Arrivals">Deferred Action
		for Childhood Arrivals</a> (DACA) program on September 5, Obama released a Facebook post criticizing the
	decision.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-497">[497]</a> Two days later, he partnered
	with former presidents <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_H._W._Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_W._Bush">George W. Bush</a> to work with <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One_America_Appeal">One America Appeal</a> to help the victims of <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey">Hurricane Harvey</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hurricane_Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> in the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States">Gulf Coast</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas">Texas</a> communities.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-498">[498]</a></p>

<p>Obama hosted the inaugural summit of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obama_Foundation">Obama
		Foundation</a> in Chicago on October 31. Obama intends for the foundation to be the central focus of his
	post-presidency and part of his ambitions for his subsequent activities following his presidency to be more
	consequential than his time in office.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-499">[499]</a>
	Obama has also been working on a Presidential memoir, in a reported $65 million deal with <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penguin_Random_House">Penguin Random House</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-nymag-500">[500]</a></p>

<p>Obama went on an international trip from November 28 to December 2, 2017, and visited China, India and France. In
	China, he delivered remarks at the Global Alliance of SMEs Summit in Shanghai and met with Chinese President <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xi_Jinping">Xi Jinping</a> in Beijing.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-501">[501]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-502">[502]</a> He then went to India, where he spoke
	at the Hindustan Times Leadership Summit before meeting with Indian Prime Minister <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narendra_Modi">Narendra Modi</a> over lunch. In addition, he held a town
	hall for young leaders, organized by the Obama Foundation.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-503">[503]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-504">[504]</a> He also met with the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalai_Lama">Dalai Lama</a> while in New Delhi.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-505">[505]</a> He ended his five-day trip in France
	where he met with French President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmanuel_Macron">Emmanuel Macron</a>,
	former President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francois_Hollande">Francois Hollande</a> and Paris Mayor <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anne_Hidalgo">Anne Hidalgo</a> and then spoke at an invitation-only event,
	touching on climate issues.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-506">[506]</a></p>

<p>Barack and Michelle Obama signed a deal on May 22, 2018 to produce docu-series, documentaries and features for <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netflix">Netflix</a> under the Obamas’ newly formed production company,
	Higher Ground Productions. On the deal, Michelle said "I have always believed in the power of storytelling to
	inspire us, to make us think differently about the world around us, and to help us open our minds and hearts to
	others."<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-507">[507]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-508">[508]</a> Higher Ground's first film, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Factory"><i>American Factory</i></a><i>,</i> was nominated for a <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Documentary_Feature">Best Documentary Oscar</a> in
	2020.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-509">[509]</a></p>

<p>A package that contained a <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_2018_United_States_mail_bombing_attempts">pipe bomb</a> was sent to
	Obama's home in Washington, D.C, on October 24, 2018. The package was intercepted by the Secret Service during
	routine mail screenings. Similar packages were sent to several other Democratic leaders, mostly those who voiced
	strong objections to the policies of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump">Donald Trump</a> and to <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CNN">CNN</a>. <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Debbie_Wasserman_Schultz">Debbie Wasserman Schultz</a> was addressed as the
	sender of the package. On October 26, 2018, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cesar_Sayoc">Cesar Sayoc</a> was
	arrested and faces five federal charges in Manhattan carrying a combined maximum sentence of 48 years behind bars in
	relation to the pipe bombs.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-510">[510]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-511">[511]</a></p>

<p>In 2019, Barack and Michelle Obama bought a home on <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard">Martha's Vineyard</a> from <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wyc_Grousbeck">Wyc Grousbeck</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-512">[512]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-513">[513]</a></p>
<h2>Legacy</h2>
<figure class="image"><img
		src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Job_Growth_by_U.S._President_-_v1.png/370px-Job_Growth_by_U.S._President_-_v1.png"
		alt=""
		srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Job_Growth_by_U.S._President_-_v1.png/555px-Job_Growth_by_U.S._President_-_v1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Job_Growth_by_U.S._President_-_v1.png/740px-Job_Growth_by_U.S._President_-_v1.png 2x"
		sizes="100vw" width="370"></figure>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>Job growth during the presidency of Obama compared to predecessors, as measured as cumulative percentage change from
	month after inauguration to end of his term</p>

<p>Obama's most significant legacy is generally considered to be the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act">Patient Protection and
		Affordable Care Act</a> (PPACA), provisions of which went into effect from 2010 to 2020. Many attempts by Senate
	Republicans to repeal the PPACA, including a "skinny repeal," have thus far failed.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-legacy-514">[514]</a> Together with the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_Care_and_Education_Reconciliation_Act">Health Care and Education
		Reconciliation Act</a> amendment, it represents the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_care_in_the_United_States">U.S. healthcare system</a>'s most
	significant regulatory overhaul and expansion of coverage since the passage of <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicare_(United_States)">Medicare</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicaid">Medicaid</a> in 1965.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Oberlander2010-515">[515]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-Blumenthal2015-516">[516]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-CohenEtAl-517">[517]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-NYTsigning-518">[518]</a></p>

<p>Many commentators credit Obama with averting a threatened <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(economics)">depression</a> and pulling the economy back from the
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Recession">Great Recession</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-legacy-514">[514]</a> According to the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Bureau_of_Labor_Statistics">U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics</a>, the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obama_administration">Obama administration</a> created 11.3&nbsp;million
	jobs from the month after <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Barack_Obama">his first
		inauguration</a> to the end of his term.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-519">[519]</a> In 2010, Obama signed into effect the
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dodd%E2%80%93Frank_Wall_Street_Reform_and_Consumer_Protection_Act">Dodd–Frank
		Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act</a>. Passed as a response to the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308">financial crisis of 2007–08</a>, it
	brought the most significant changes to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_regulation">financial
		regulation</a> in the United States since the regulatory reform that followed the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression">Great Depression</a> under Democratic President <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-520">[520]</a></p>

<p>In 2009, Obama signed into law the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Defense_Authorization_Act_for_Fiscal_Year_2010">National Defense
		Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2010</a>, which contained in it the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthew_Shepard_and_James_Byrd_Jr._Hate_Crimes_Prevention_Act">Matthew
		Shepard and James Byrd Jr. Hate Crimes Prevention Act</a>, the first addition to existing federal hate crime law
	in the United States since Democratic President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton">Bill
		Clinton</a> signed into law the Church Arson Prevention Act of 1996. The Matthew Shepard and James Byrd Jr. Hate
	Crimes Prevention Act expanded <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hate_crime_laws_in_the_United_States">existing
		federal hate crime laws in the United States</a> to apply to crimes motivated by a victim's actual or perceived
	gender, sexual orientation, gender identity, or disability, and dropped the prerequisite that the victim be engaging
	in a federally protected activity.</p>

<p>As president, Obama advanced LGBT rights.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-521">[521]</a>
	In 2010, he signed the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don%27t_Ask,_Don%27t_Tell_Repeal_Act_of_2010">Don't
		Ask, Don't Tell Repeal Act</a>, which brought an end to "<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don%27t_ask,_don%27t_tell">don't ask, don't tell</a>" policy in the U.S.
	armed forces that banned open service from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lesbian,_gay_and_bisexual">LGB</a>
	people; the law went into effect the following year.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-522">[522]</a> In 2016, his administration brought an
	end to the ban on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transgender">transgender</a> people serving openly in the
	U.S. armed forces.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-523">[523]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-TransBan1-234">[234]</a> A <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallup_poll">Gallup poll</a>, taken in the final days of Obama's term,
	showed that 68% of Americans believed the U.S. had made progress in the situation for gays and lesbians during
	Obama's eight years in office.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-524">[524]</a></p>

<p>Obama substantially escalated the use of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drone_strikes">drone strikes</a>
	against suspected militants and terrorists associated with <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> and the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taliban">Taliban</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-525">[525]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-526">[526]</a> In 2016, the last year of his
	presidency, the US dropped 26,171 bombs on seven different countries.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-527">[527]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-528">[528]</a> Obama left about 8,400 US troops in <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, 5,262 in Iraq, 503 in Syria, 133 in Pakistan,
	106 in Somalia, seven in Yemen, and two in Libya at the end of his presidency.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-529">[529]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-530">[530]</a></p>

<p>According to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pew_Research_Center">Pew Research Center</a> and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Bureau_of_Justice_Statistics">United States Bureau of Justice
		Statistics</a>, from December 31, 2009, to December 31, 2015, inmates sentenced in US federal custody declined
	by five percent. This is the largest decline in sentenced inmates in US federal custody since Democratic President
	<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>. By contrast, the federal prison population
	increased significantly under presidents <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_H._W._Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>, <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, and <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_W._Bush">George W. Bush</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-531">[531]</a></p>

<p>Obama left office in January 2017 with a 60% approval rating.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-532">[532]</a><a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-533">[533]</a> A 2018 survey of historians by the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Political_Science_Association">American Political Science
		Association</a> ranked Obama the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_presidents_of_the_United_States">8th-greatest
		American President</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-How_Does_Trump_Stack_Up_Against_the_Best%E2%80%94and_Worst%E2%80%94Presidents?-4">[4]</a>
	Obama gained 10 spots from the same survey in 2015 from the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brookings_Institution">Brookings Institution</a> that ranked Obama the
	18th-greatest American President.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-534">[534]</a></p>
<h3><strong>Presidential library</strong></h3>

<p><i>Main article: </i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama_Presidential_Center"><i>Barack Obama
			Presidential Center</i></a></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p>The Barack Obama Presidential Center is Obama's planned <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_library">presidential library</a>. It will be hosted by the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Chicago">University of Chicago</a> and located in <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jackson_Park_(Chicago)">Jackson Park</a> on the <a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Side,_Chicago">South Side of Chicago</a>.<a
		href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama#cite_note-535">[535]</a></p>
